//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/PR_secondary_123.svg/62px-PR_secondary_123.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_146" title="Puerto Rico Highway 146"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/PR_secondary_146.svg/31px-PR_secondary_146.svg.png" decoding="async" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/PR_secondary_146.svg/62px-PR_secondary_146.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="600" /></a></span><br /><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_22" title="Puerto Rico Highway 22"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Toll_plate_yellow.svg/25px-Toll_plate_yellow.svg.png" decoding="async" width="25" height="13" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Toll_plate_yellow.svg/38px-Toll_plate_yellow.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Toll_plate_yellow.svg/50px-Toll_plate_yellow.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="601" data-file-height="301" /></a></span><br /><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_22" title="Puerto Rico Highway 22"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/PR_primary_22.svg/25px-PR_primary_22.svg.png" decoding="async" width="25" height="25" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/PR_primary_22.svg/38px-PR_primary_22.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/PR_primary_22.svg/50px-PR_primary_22.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="601" data-file-height="601" /></a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Arecibo</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xcb\x8c/: secondary stress follows">\xcb\x8c</span><span title="/\xc3\xa6r/: &#39;arr&#39; in &#39;marry&#39;">\xc3\xa6r</span><span title="/\xc9\x99/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">\xc9\x99</span><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span><span title="/i\xcb\x90/: &#39;ee&#39; in &#39;fleece&#39;">i\xcb\x90</span><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="/o\xca\x8a/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;code&#39;">o\xca\x8a</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1177148991">.mw-parser-output .IPA-label-small{font-size:85%}.mw-parser-output .references .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .infobox .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .navbox .IPA-label-small{font-size:100%}</style><span class="IPA-label IPA-label-small">Spanish pronunciation:</span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="es-Latn-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">&#91;a\xc9\xbee\xcb\x88si\xce\xb2o&#93;</a></span>) is a <a href="/wiki/Arecibo_barrio-pueblo" title="Arecibo barrio-pueblo">city</a> and <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Municipalities of Puerto Rico">municipality</a> on the northern coast of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, on the shores of the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>, located north of <a href="/wiki/Utuado,_Puerto_Rico" title="Utuado, Puerto Rico">Utuado</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ciales,_Puerto_Rico" title="Ciales, Puerto Rico">Ciales</a>; east of <a href="/wiki/Hatillo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Hatillo, Puerto Rico">Hatillo</a>; and west of <a href="/wiki/Barceloneta,_Puerto_Rico" title="Barceloneta, Puerto Rico">Barceloneta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Florida,_Puerto_Rico" title="Florida, Puerto Rico">Florida</a>. It is about 50 miles (80&#160;km) west of <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan</a>, the capital city. Arecibo is the largest municipality in <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> by area, and it is the core city of the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_statistical_areas" title="Puerto Rico statistical areas">Arecibo Metropolitan Statistical Area</a> and part of the greater <a href="/wiki/San_Juan%E2%80%93Caguas%E2%80%93Guaynabo_metropolitan_area" title="San Juan\xe2\x80\x93Caguas\xe2\x80\x93Guaynabo metropolitan area">San Juan\xe2\x80\x93Bayam\xc3\xb3n, PR</a> <a href="/wiki/Combined_statistical_area" title="Combined statistical area">Combined Statistical Area</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It is spread over 18 <i>barrios</i> and <a href="/wiki/Arecibo_barrio-pueblo" title="Arecibo barrio-pueblo">Arecibo Pueblo</a> (the downtown area and the administrative center of the city). Its population in 2020 was 87,754.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Arecibo_Observatory" title="Arecibo Observatory">Arecibo Observatory</a>, which housed the <a href="/wiki/Arecibo_telescope" class="mw-redirect" title="Arecibo telescope">Arecibo telescope</a>, the world\'s largest radio telescope until July 2016, is located in the municipality. The Arecibo telescope collapsed on December 1, 2020. Arecibo is the seat of the Roman Catholic <a href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Arecibo" class="mw-redirect" title="Diocese of Arecibo">Diocese of Arecibo</a>.\n</p>\n<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Etymology_and_nicknames">Etymology and nicknames</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arecibo,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology and nicknames"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The name <i>Arecibo</i> comes from the <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Ta\xc3\xadno people">Ta\xc3\xadno</a> chief <a href="/wiki/Arasibo" title="Arasibo">Xamaica Arasibo</a>, cacique of the <i>yucayeque</i> (Ta\xc3\xadno settlement) of <b>Abacoa</b> where the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Spanish colonization of the Americas">Spanish</a> town of <a href="/wiki/Arecibo_barrio-pueblo" title="Arecibo barrio-pueblo">Arecibo</a> was settled in 1556. The word <i>Arasibo</i> itself most likely comes from the <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_language" title="Ta\xc3\xadno language">Ta\xc3\xadno</a> words <i>ara</i>, possibly meaning or related to "people", and <i>siba</i>, most likely meaning "rock" or "stone". This name also lends itself to the name of the <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Grande_de_Arecibo" title="R\xc3\xado Grande de Arecibo">river</a> which flows through the municipality into the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Some of the city\'s nicknames are: <i>Villa del Capit\xc3\xa1n Correa</i> ("Villa of Captain Correa"), after <a href="/wiki/Antonio_de_los_Reyes_Correa" title="Antonio de los Reyes Correa">Captain Antonio de los Reyes Correa</a>, a Spanish soldier who famously and successfully defended the city from a British invasion; <i>La Muy Leal</i> ("the very loyal [one]") after the title often granted to Spanish colonial cities; and <i>Diamante del Norte</i> ("<a href="/wiki/Diamond" title="Diamond">Diamond</a> of the North") due to the city\'s location in the northern coast of the island.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arecibo,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Smithsonian_1901_map_of_Puerto_Rico_caciques.png" class="mw-file-description" title="Smithsonian map of Puerto Rico caciques"><img alt="Smithsonian map of Puerto Rico caciques" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Smithsonian_1901_map_of_Puerto_Rico_caciques.png/300px-Smithsonian_1901_map_of_Puerto_Rico_caciques.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="235" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Smithsonian_1901_map_of_Puerto_Rico_caciques.png/450px-Smithsonian_1901_map_of_Puerto_Rico_caciques.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/48/Smithsonian_1901_map_of_Puerto_Rico_caciques.png 2x" data-file-width="523" data-file-height="410" /></a><figcaption>Smithsonian map of Puerto Rico caciques</figcaption></figure>\n<p>When the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish</a> arrived, they found the area occupied by the indigenous <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Ta\xc3\xadno people">Ta\xc3\xadno</a>, led by Xamaica <a href="/wiki/Arasibo" title="Arasibo">Arasibo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cacique" title="Cacique">Cacique</a> (chief) of the <i>yucayeque</i> (town) then named Abacoa.<sup id="cite_ref-PR_Ency_Founding_Symbols_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PR_Ency_Founding_Symbols-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-taino-tribe.org_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-taino-tribe.org-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Spanish colonists settled Arecibo in 1556, which they named for the cacique. It was their fourth settlement on the island, after <a href="/wiki/Caparra_Archaeological_Site" title="Caparra Archaeological Site">Caparra</a> (which later became <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan</a>), <a href="/wiki/San_German,_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="San German, Puerto Rico">San German</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Coamo" class="mw-redirect" title="Coamo">Coamo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Arecibo was officially founded as a town<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> by the Spanish crown on May 1, 1616, under the governorship of Captain <a href="/w/index.php?title=Felipe_de_Beaumont_y_Navarra&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Felipe de Beaumont y Navarra (page does not exist)">Felipe de Beaumont y Navarra</a>, when the <a href="/wiki/King_of_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="King of Spain">King of Spain</a> granted the land (and the <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Ta\xc3\xadno people">Taino</a> living there) to Lope Conchillos.<sup id="cite_ref-PR_Ency_Founding_Symbols_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PR_Ency_Founding_Symbols-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>For some time the island was competed for by other European powers. On August 5, 1702, <a href="/wiki/Captain_(land)" class="mw-redirect" title="Captain (land)">Captain</a> <a href="/wiki/Antonio_de_los_Reyes_Correa" title="Antonio de los Reyes Correa">Antonio de los Reyes Correa</a>, a member of the <a href="/wiki/Military_history_of_Spain" title="Military history of Spain">Spanish Army</a>, successfully defended Arecibo from a <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">British</a> Navy invasion led by rear-admiral <a href="/wiki/William_Whetstone" title="William Whetstone">William Whetstone</a>. Commanding two <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">British Navy</a> ships and 40 men, Whetstone tried to take control of the city. Correa ambushed his forces, killing 22 British seamen and driving them off. The Spanish defenders suffered only one death and three wounded soldiers. This gave the city its nickname <i>The Village of Captain Correa</i> (<i>La Villa del Capitan Correa</i>)\n</p><p>In 1778, Arecibo, by royal decree, was awarded the "Villa" status, though it was not integrated as such until 1802. In 1850 it was awarded the "Muy Leal" (very loyal) title.<sup id="cite_ref-Cr\xc3\xb3nicas_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cr\xc3\xb3nicas-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Over time, large part of its territory became separate municipalities. These include <a href="/wiki/Manati" class="mw-redirect" title="Manati">Manati</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barceloneta,_Puerto_Rico" title="Barceloneta, Puerto Rico">Barceloneta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florida,_Puerto_Rico" title="Florida, Puerto Rico">Florida</a>, <a href="/wiki/Utuado" class="mw-redirect" title="Utuado">Utuado</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jayuya" class="mw-redirect" title="Jayuya">Jayuya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hatillo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Hatillo, Puerto Rico">Hatillo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Camuy" class="mw-redirect" title="Camuy">Camuy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quebradillas" class="mw-redirect" title="Quebradillas">Quebradillas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Isabela,_Puerto_Rico" title="Isabela, Puerto Rico">Isabela</a>. In 1982, it was promoted to city status, though it continued to be known by its previous nickname.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Maria</a> on September 20, 2017, triggered extensive flooding, and damage to infrastructure with over 3,000 people losing their homes. Two hospitals were damaged and the hurricane caused <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria_death_toll_controversy" title="Hurricane Maria death toll controversy">deaths</a> as well.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Geography">Geography</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arecibo,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Geography"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Arecibo is located in the Northern Coastal Plain region of Puerto Rico, extending inland into the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Karst_(Puerto_Rico)" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Karst (Puerto Rico)">Northern Karst</a> region. It lies on the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>; north of <a href="/wiki/Utuado" class="mw-redirect" title="Utuado">Utuado</a>; east of <a href="/wiki/Hatillo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Hatillo, Puerto Rico">Hatillo</a>; and west of <a href="/wiki/Barceloneta,_Puerto_Rico" title="Barceloneta, Puerto Rico">Barceloneta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Florida,_Puerto_Rico" title="Florida, Puerto Rico">Florida</a>. The city occupies an area of 127 square miles (330&#160;km<sup>2</sup>), of which, 45.23&#160;sq&#160;mi (117.1&#160;km<sup>2</sup>), is water.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PR_Ency_General_Info_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PR_Ency_General_Info-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Rio_Grande_de_Arecibo" class="mw-redirect" title="Rio Grande de Arecibo">Rio Grande de Arecibo</a> is the main river in the municipality, running through the middle of it. South of the municipality, in the <a href="/wiki/Karst" title="Karst">karst</a> region, it forms the <a href="/wiki/Lago_Dos_Bocas" class="mw-redirect" title="Lago Dos Bocas">Dos Bocas Lake</a>, a primary source of water for Northern Puerto Rico. Several rivers feed the Rio Grande, including the <a href="/wiki/Tanam%C3%A1_River" title="Tanam\xc3\xa1 River">Tanama River</a>. Ca\xc3\xb1o Santiago is an artificial canal created in the 19th century by partially diverting the Tanama River\'s waters tobarrios a small temporary stream, to supply water to poor neighborhoods in Arecibo, discharging into the Arecibo River near its own mouth. In the 1950s it was modified to pass slightly more south of the city center. Poor maintenance, sediment and pollution has turned the canal once again into a temporary stream. East of the river lies <a href="/wiki/Ca%C3%B1o_Tiburones" title="Ca\xc3\xb1o Tiburones">Ca\xc3\xb1o Tiburones</a>, an important marshland area that provides habitat for many kinds of birds and wildlife.\n</p><p>Arecibo has two forest reserves. <a href="/wiki/Cambalache_State_Forest" class="mw-redirect" title="Cambalache State Forest">Cambalache State Forest</a> is located along the <a href="/wiki/Barceloneta,_Puerto_Rico" title="Barceloneta, Puerto Rico">Barceloneta</a> municipal limits, while <a href="/wiki/Rio_Abajo_State_Forest" class="mw-redirect" title="Rio Abajo State Forest">Rio Abajo State Forest</a> is located between Arecibo and <a href="/wiki/Utuado,_Puerto_Rico" title="Utuado, Puerto Rico">Utuado</a>. Caves include <a href="/wiki/Cueva_Ventana" title="Cueva Ventana">Cueva Ventana</a>, which overlooks the valley formed by the Rio Grande de Arecibo, and <a href="/wiki/Cueva_del_Indio_(Arecibo)" title="Cueva del Indio (Arecibo)">Cueva del Indio</a> (Cave of the Indian), where paintings made by prehistoric <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples" title="Indigenous peoples">indigenous peoples</a> have been seen.\n</p><p>Environmental impact studies have been done to consider remedies for <a href="/wiki/Flood" title="Flood">flooding</a> that often occurs in Arecibo.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Barrios">Barrios</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arecibo,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Barrios"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Arecibo,_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Arecibo%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png/220px-Arecibo%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="164" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Arecibo%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png/330px-Arecibo%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Arecibo%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png/440px-Arecibo%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png 2x" data-file-width="847" data-file-height="630" /></a><figcaption>Subdivisions of Arecibo</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Like all municipalities of Puerto Rico, Arecibo is subdivided into <a href="/wiki/Barrios_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Barrios of Puerto Rico">barrios</a>. The municipal buildings, central square and large Catholic church are located in a small barrio referred to as <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">"el pueblo"</i></span>, near the center of the municipality.<sup id="cite_ref-Law2015_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law2015-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1184024115">.mw-parser-output .div-col{margin-top:0.3em;column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .div-col-small{font-size:90%}.mw-parser-output .div-col dd{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}</style><div class="div-col" style="column-width: 15em;">\n<ol><li><a href="/wiki/Arecibo_barrio-pueblo" title="Arecibo href="/wiki/Tanam%C3%A1,_Arecibo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Tanam\xc3\xa1, Arecibo, Puerto Rico">Tanam\xc3\xa1</a></li></ol>\n</div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Sectors">Sectors</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arecibo,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Sectors"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_barrios_and_sectors_of_Arecibo,_Puerto_Rico" title="List of barrios and sectors of Arecibo, Puerto Rico">List of barrios and sectors of Arecibo, Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<p>Barrios (which for US census purposes, are like <a href="/wiki/Minor_civil_divisions" class="mw-redirect" title="Minor civil divisions">minor civil divisions</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-Barrio-Pueblo_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Barrio-Pueblo-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> in turn are further subdivided into smaller local populated place areas/units called <b>sectores</b> (<i>sectors</i> in English). The types of <i>sectores</i> may vary, from normally <i>sector</i> to <i>urbanizaci\xc3\xb3n</i> to <i>reparto</i> to <i>barriada</i> to <i>residencial</i>, among others.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Law_1-2001_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law_1-2001-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Special_Communities">Special Communities</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arecibo,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Special Communities"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Office_for_Socioeconomic_and_Community_Development" title="Puerto Rico Office for Socioeconomic and Community Development">Puerto Rico Office for Socioeconomic and Community Development</a></div>\n<p><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Comunidades Especiales de Puerto Rico</i></span> (Special Communities of Puerto Rico) are marginalized communities whose citizens are experiencing a certain amount of <a href="/wiki/Social_exclusion" title="Social exclusion">social exclusion</a>. A map shows these communities occur in nearly every municipality of the commonwealth. Of the 742 places that were on the list in 2014, the following barrios, communities, sectors, or neighborhoods were in Arecibo: \n<span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Animas \xe2\x80\x93 Factor 1, Sector Los Muertos in Arrozal, Sector El Jobo in Rio Arriba, Sector El Valle in Rio Arriba, Buenos Aires (Magallanes), Calichoza, Canta Gallo, Carreras, Cruz Roja, El Cerro \xe2\x80\x93 Factor 1, Abra San Francisco, El Vig\xc3\xada, Esperanza (Cienagueta), La Planta, Palo Blanco,</i></span>  and <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Sector Carolina in Sabana Hoyos</i></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Climate">Climate</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arecibo,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Climate"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Tropical monsoon climate, occasionally also known as a tropical wet climate or tropical monsoon and trade-wind littoral climate in climate classification, is a relatively rare type of climate. The K\xc3\xb6ppen Climate Classification subtype for this climate is "<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification#Group_A:_Tropical/megathermal_climates" title="K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification">Am</a>". (Tropical Monsoon Climate).<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div>\n<table class="wikitable mw-collapsible mw-collapsed" style="width:auto; text-align:center; line-height:1.2em;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Tourism">Tourism</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arecibo,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Tourism"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Landmarks_and_places_of_interest">Landmarks and places of interest</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arecibo,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Landmarks and places of interest"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The Arecibo Harbor is managed by the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Ports_Authority" title="Puerto Rico Ports Authority">Puerto Rico Ports Authority</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Harbor_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harbor-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Catedral_de_Arecibo_2.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Catedral_de_Arecibo_2.jpg/220px-Catedral_de_Arecibo_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Catedral_de_Arecibo_2.jpg/330px-Catedral_de_Arecibo_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Catedral_de_Arecibo_2.jpg/440px-Catedral_de_Arecibo_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a><figcaption>Cathedral of Saint Phillip Apostle in Arecibo barrio-pueblo</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Arecibo is one of the oldest <a href="/wiki/Spanish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Spanish colonization of the Americas">colonial</a> towns in <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> (1616). Among its historic buildings is the <a href="/wiki/Catedral_de_San_Felipe_Ap%C3%B3stol_(Arecibo,_Puerto_Rico)" title="Catedral de San Felipe Ap\xc3\xb3stol (Arecibo, Puerto Rico)">Cathedral of Saint Philip the Apostle</a>, built beginning in the late 18th century. The first church, built in the middle of the 17th century, was destroyed by an <a href="/wiki/1787_Boricua_earthquake" title="1787 Boricua earthquake">earthquake in 1787</a>. Construction of its replacement began soon after, although it was not completed until 1846. Four days after its dedication, another earthquake seriously damaged it. Repairs were not completed until 1882. The <a href="/wiki/1918_San_Ferm%C3%ADn_earthquake" title="1918 San Ferm\xc3\xadn earthquake">1918 earthquake</a> damaged the vault so badly that it was replaced by a flat concrete roof; a vaulted ceiling of composition board was placed inside.\n</p><p>The cathedral of Arecibo is Puerto Rico\'s second-largest church after the <a href="/wiki/Catedral_Metropolitana_Bas%C3%ADlica_de_San_Juan_Bautista_(San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico)" class="mw-redirect" title="Catedral Metropolitana Bas\xc3\xadlica de San Juan Bautista (San Juan, Puerto Rico)">Cathedral of San Juan</a>. The plan is rectangular with three <a href="/wiki/Nave" title="Nave">naves</a>; the side naves are cut short to allow large flanking chapels, which occupy almost half the length of the church. The <a href="/wiki/Apse" title="Apse">apse</a> is semicircular, and has an unusual half-dome covering it. The facade is a triangular composition of three stages. The top stage, a short central tower, is a later addition, according to local architects and historians. <a href="/wiki/Neoclassical_architecture" title="Neoclassical architecture">Neoclassic</a> ornamentation is used in an academic fashion on the lowest stage, but the other two show a less traditional use of bands and <a href="/wiki/Pilaster" title="Pilaster">pilasters</a>. The Renaissance-style windows are uncommon in Puerto Rican churches, but the central tower over the entrance is a common motif used throughout the island.\n</p>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Arecibo_town_hall.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Arecibo_town_hall.jpg/220px-Arecibo_town_hall.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Arecibo_town_hall.jpg/330px-Arecibo_town_hall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Arecibo_town_hall.jpg/440px-Arecibo_town_hall.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2448" data-file-height="3264" /></a><figcaption>Arecibo City Hall</figcaption></figure>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Casa_Alcald%C3%ADa_de_Arecibo" title="Casa Alcald\xc3\xada de Arecibo">City Hall</a>, built in 1866, served as jail to revolutionaries of <i><a href="/wiki/El_Grito_de_Lares" class="mw-redirect" title="El Grito de Lares">El Grito de Lares</a></i> in 1868. In the 1918 earthquake, the frontal section of the building was destroyed. When repairs were made, a tower and clock were added to the building. In 1978, the building was restored to its original form.\n</p><p>The City Hall of Arecibo is typical of these regional seats of government. It is relatively modest in size, of stuccoed masonry, with an academically correct composition, having a pedimented center pavilion which projects slightly. The lower story is rusticated, with arched openings; the three doorways in the center giving the effect of a <i><a href="/wiki/Loggia" title="Loggia">loggia</a>.</i> The upper windows all have segmental pediments and balconies; the central trio share one long balcony. Architectural detailing is modest, but the building is graceful and charming.\n</p><p>In 1898 the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish people">Spaniards</a> built the <a href="/wiki/Arecibo_Light" title="Arecibo Light">Punta Los Morrillos Lighthouse</a>. It was automated in 1964 and is still in use. A small park, Arecibo Lighthouse and Historical Park, has been established around it.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Arecibo_Observatory" title="Arecibo Observatory">Arecibo Observatory</a> was the home of <a href="/wiki/Arecibo_telescope" class="mw-redirect" title="Arecibo telescope">Arecibo telescope</a>, once the largest single-aperture radio telescope ever constructed and one of the world\'s most powerful radar-radio telescopes. The observatory\'s purpose was to support scientific studies. It attracted several <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_(film_industry)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hollywood (film industry)">Hollywood</a> directors who have filmed there; most recently <i><a href="/wiki/GoldenEye" title="GoldenEye">GoldenEye</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Contact_(1997_American_film)" title="Contact (1997 American film)">Contact</a></i>. The radio telescope was used in 1974 to send the <a href="/wiki/Arecibo_message" title="Arecibo message">Arecibo message</a> to space. The telescope collapsed in 2020.\nCasa Ulanga was originally a residence built by Spanish immigrant Francisco Ulanga, and has served multiple uses over the years. It was used as a bank, store, city hall of Arecibo, hospital, jail, tribunal, and is now operated as the Arecibo Cultural Center.\n</p>\n<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Cueva_del_Indio_aerial,_PR.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Cueva_del_Indio_aerial%2C_PR.jpg/220px-Cueva_del_Indio_aerial%2C_PR.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Cueva_del_Indio_aerial%2C_PR.jpg/330px-Cueva_del_Indio_aerial%2C_PR.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Cueva_del_Indio_aerial%2C_PR.jpg/440px-Cueva_del_Indio_aerial%2C_PR.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1400" data-file-height="938" /></a><figcaption>Aerial view of <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Cueva del Indio</i></span>, <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">&#8201;1967</span></figcaption></figure>\n<p><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Cueva del Indio</i></span> is an <a href="/wiki/Archeological_site" class="mw-redirect" title="Archeological site">archeological site</a> where <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Ta\xc3\xadno people">Ta\xc3\xadno</a> drawings can be found.\n</p><p>The "<a href="/wiki/Birth_of_the_New_World" title="Birth of the New World">Birth of the New World</a>" is a statue depicting <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a> and is located in <a href="/wiki/Islote,_Arecibo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Islote, Arecibo, Puerto Rico">Islote</a>, Arecibo.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 295&#160;ft (90&#160;m). The statue is the work of Russian sculptor <a href="/wiki/Zurab_Tsereteli" title="Zurab Tsereteli">Zurab Tsereteli</a>, and it is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_tallest_statues_in_the_United_States" title="List of the tallest statues in the United States">tallest statue</a> in the Americas.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Other places of interest in Arecibo include:\n</p>\n<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/Cambalache_Forest_Reserve" title="Cambalache Forest Reserve">Cambalache Forest Reserve</a></li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/Lago_Dos_Bocas" class="mw-redirect" title="Lago Dos Bocas">Dos Bocas Lake</a></b> which is a reservoir located between the municipalities of Arecibo and <a href="/wiki/Utuado,_Puerto_Rico" title="Utuado, Puerto Rico">Utuado</a>.</li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/Paseo_V%C3%ADctor_Rojas" title="Paseo V\xc3\xadctor Rojas">Paseo Victor Rojas</a></b> (Victor Rojas Walk) also known as <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Paseo de Damas</i></span> or simply <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">El Fuerte</i></span>, was built in 1881 where the Fort San Miguel\'s ruins once were</li>\n<li><b>Manuel "Petaca" Iguina Coliseum</b> which is home of the <a href="/wiki/Arecibo_Captains" class="mw-redirect" title="Arecibo Captains">Arecibo Captains</a> basketball team.</li></ul>\n<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Museo_de_Arte_e_Historia_de_Arecibo,_Puerto_Rico_-_panoramio.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Museo_de_Arte_e_Historia_de_Arecibo%2C_Puerto_Rico_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-Museo_de_Arte_e_Historia_de_Arecibo%2C_Puerto_Rico_-_panoramio.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Museo_de_Arte_e_Historia_de_Arecibo%2C_Puerto_Rico_-_panoramio.jpg/330px-Museo_de_Arte_e_Historia_de_Arecibo%2C_Puerto_Rico_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Museo_de_Arte_e_Historia_de_Arecibo%2C_Puerto_Rico_-_panoramio.jpg/440px-Museo_de_Arte_e_Historia_de_Arecibo%2C_Puerto_Rico_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3744" data-file-height="2104" /></a><figcaption>Museum of Art and History of Arecibo</figcaption></figure>\n<ul><li><b>Museum of Art and History of Arecibo</b> which has art from local artists and shows the city\'s history</li></ul>\n<p>Arecibo beaches include Los Morillos, Los Negritos, Poza del Obispo, and Las Tunas. <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Pozo del Obispo</i></span> Beach in Arecibo is considered a dangerous beach.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>To stimulate local tourism during the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_Puerto_Rico" title="COVID-19 pandemic in Puerto Rico">COVID-19 pandemic in Puerto Rico</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Tourism_Company" title="Puerto Rico Tourism Company">Puerto Rico Tourism Company</a> launched the <i>Voy Turistiendo</i> (I\'m Touring) campaign in 2021. The campaign featured a passport book with a page for each municipality. The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Voy Turisteando</i></span> Arecibo passport page lists <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Cueva Ventana</i></span>, <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Museo Casa Trina Padilla de Sanz</i></span>, and the Arecibo Light House and Historical Park, as places of interest.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Culture">Culture</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arecibo,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Culture"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Festivals_and_events">Festivals and events</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arecibo,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Festivals and events"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Arecibo began celebrating its patron saint festival in 1616.<sup id="cite_ref-Album_Historico_de_Arecibo_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Album_Historico_de_Arecibo-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Arecibo celebrates its <a href="/wiki/Fiestas_patronales_in_Puerto_Rico" title="Fiestas patronales in Puerto Rico">patron saint</a> festival in May. The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Fiestas Patronales de San Felipe Apostol</i></span> is a religious and cultural celebration that generally features parades, games, artisans, amusement rides, regional food, and live entertainment.<sup id="cite_ref-PR_Ency_General_Info_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PR_Ency_General_Info-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> \n</p><p>Other festivals and events celebrated in Arecibo include:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Bicycle competition \xe2\x80\x93 January</li>\n<li><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Festival de Paracaidismo</i></span> (Parachuting festival) \xe2\x80\x93 February<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>Arecibo Carnival \xe2\x80\x93 February</li>\n<li>Folklore Festival \xe2\x80\x93 July</li>\n<li>Beach festival \xe2\x80\x93 July</li>\n<li>Artisan Fair \xe2\x80\x93 September</li>\n<li>Cet\xc3\xad Festival \xe2\x80\x93 November</li>\n<li>Centennial of the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Flag of Puerto Rico">Puerto Rican flag</a> \xe2\x80\x93 December</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Sports">Sports</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arecibo,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Sports"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Arecibo has two professional sports franchises, the <a href="/wiki/Lobos_de_Arecibo" title="Lobos de Arecibo">Lobos de Arecibo</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Liga_de_B%C3%A9isbol_Profesional_Roberto_Clemente" title="Liga de B\xc3\xa9isbol Profesional Roberto Clemente">Roberto Clemente Professional Baseball League</a> (a.k.a. Liga de B\xc3\xa9isbol Profesional Roberto Clemente or LBPRC), and the <a href="/wiki/Capitanes_de_Arecibo" title="Capitanes de Arecibo">Capitanes de Arecibo</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Baloncesto_Superior_Nacional" title="Baloncesto Superior Nacional">National Superior Basketball League</a> (Baloncesto Superior Nacional or BSN).\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Baseball">Baseball</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arecibo,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Baseball"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The Lobos won the 1983 then-known Liga de B\xc3\xa9isbol Profesional de Puerto Rico (LBPPR) national baseball championship and the 1983 <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_World_Series" class="mw-redirect" title="Caribbean World Series">Caribbean World Series</a>, the only time the franchise won both titles. At that time, they had <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">MLB</a> prospect <a href="/wiki/Dickie_Thon" title="Dickie Thon">Dickie Thon</a>, then also of the <a href="/wiki/Houston_Astros" title="Houston Astros">Houston Astros</a>, on their roster. Thon then suffered a life-threatening and career-affecting eye injury during an Astros game in 1984. The Lobos won a championship again in 1996.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Basketball">Basketball</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arecibo,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Basketball"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The Capitanes won their first ever BSN national championship in 1959. After that, the Capitanes have not had much luck in their basketball tournaments for the next few decades. However, that would begin to change in 2002, as they started to turn things around, by reaching the BSN semifinals; yet they lost the series to the <a href="/wiki/Vaqueros_de_Bayam%C3%B3n" title="Vaqueros de Bayam\xc3\xb3n">Vaqueros de Bayam\xc3\xb3n</a> by losing four straight games, after having a 3\xe2\x80\x930 series lead, thus failing their chances to make into the finals. In 2005, the Capitanes won the BSN national championship by defeating the Vaqueros de Bayam\xc3\xb3n in a four-game sweep. This was the first championship in 46 years. In 2007 they got to the finals, losing in the overtime on the seventh game of the series against the <a href="/wiki/Cangrejeros_de_Santurce_(basketball)" title="Cangrejeros de Santurce (basketball)">Cangrejeros de Santurce</a>. In 2008 Arecibo won their third BSN national championship, this time against the <a href="/wiki/Gigantes_de_Carolina_(men%27s_basketball)" title="Gigantes de Carolina (men&#39;s basketball)">Gigantes de Carolina</a>. In 2010, they won their fourth BSN national title in six seasons, this time against the Vaqueros de Bayam\xc3\xb3n.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Radio_stations">Radio stations</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arecibo,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Radio stations"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/WCMN-FM" title="WCMN-FM">WCMN-FM</a> \xe2\x80\x93 Hot 102 107.3 FM (re-transmitter)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/WCMN-AM" class="mw-redirect" title="WCMN-AM">WCMN-AM</a> \xe2\x80\x93 NotiUno 1280 AM</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/WNIK-FM" title="WNIK-FM">WNIK-FM</a> \xe2\x80\x93 Super K 106 FM</li>\n<li>WNIK-AM \xe2\x80\x93 Radio Unica</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/WMIA_(AM)" title="WMIA (AM)">WMIA-AM</a> \xe2\x80\x93 MIA Radio Arecibo 1070 AM <sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Economy">Economy</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arecibo,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Economy"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:20180315-OC-PJK-0742_TONED_(40991530032).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/20180315-OC-PJK-0742_TONED_%2840991530032%29.jpg/220px-20180315-OC-PJK-0742_TONED_%2840991530032%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/20180315-OC-PJK-0742_TONED_%2840991530032%29.jpg/330px-20180315-OC-PJK-0742_TONED_%2840991530032%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/20180315-OC-PJK-0742_TONED_%2840991530032%29.jpg/440px-20180315-OC-PJK-0742_TONED_%2840991530032%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a><figcaption>Vaqueria Ceiba Del Mar</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Arecibo\'s economy is diverse with pharmaceuticals, agriculture and fishing.<sup id="cite_ref-PR_Ency_General_Info_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PR_Ency_General_Info-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Vaqueria Ceiba Del Mar is located in Arecibo and is one of the largest on the island of Puerto Rico. They also have operations in <a href="/wiki/Hatillo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Hatillo, Puerto Rico">Hatillo</a>. After <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Maria</a>, the farm had to consolidate their three operations into one.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Business">Business</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arecibo,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Business"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Arecibo\'s main shopping mall is <a href="/w/index.php?title=Plaza_del_Atlantico&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Plaza del Atlantico (page does not exist)">Plaza del Atlantico</a> as well as the one situated in the neighboring town of <a href="/wiki/Hatillo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Hatillo, Puerto Rico">Hatillo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plaza_del_Norte" title="Plaza del Norte">Plaza del Norte</a>.\n</p><p>In 2021, Hilton was constructing a hotel in Arecibo.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Industrial">Industrial</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arecibo,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Industrial"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Arecibo is home to Fortune 500 corporations such as <a href="/wiki/Merck_%26_Co." title="Merck &amp; Co.">Merck</a>, <a href="/wiki/General_Electric" title="General Electric">General Electric</a>. Other important companies are Thermo King Corporation, Eaton, Los Cidrines, Expressway Eco Printing, Arecibo Tropical Flag and ABB.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Demographics">Demographics</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arecibo,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" census">1960</a></th><td>69,879</td><td></td><td>\xe2\x88\x927.3%</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/1970_United_States_census" title="1970 United States census">2020</a></th><td>87,754</td><td></td><td>\xe2\x88\x929.0%</td></tr><tr><td colspan="4" class="us-census-pop-footnote" style="text-align: center">U.S. Decennial Census<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><br />1899 (shown as 1900)<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 1910\xe2\x80\x931930<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><br />1930\xe2\x80\x931950<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 1960\xe2\x80\x932000<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 2010<sup id="cite_ref-2010_Census_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010_Census-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n2020<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></td></tr>\n</tbody></table><p>According to the 2010 Census the municipality of Arecibo is 99% <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans" title="Hispanic and Latino Americans">Hispanic</a> of which 78% identifies as white (of <a href="/wiki/White_Puerto_Ricans" title="White Puerto Ricans">European</a> descent), 4.6% black (<a href="/wiki/Afro%E2%80%93Puerto_Ricans" title="Afro\xe2\x80\x93Puerto Ricans">Afro-Puerto Rican</a> descent), and 1.2% with two or more races.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The majority of the population is mostly of <a href="/wiki/Spaniards" title="Spaniards">Spanish</a> descent, but there has been intermarriage with more recent groups from other parts of Europe, with some having Middle Eastern, <a href="/wiki/French_immigration_to_Puerto_Rico" title="French immigration to Puerto Rico">French</a>, Italian, American or of other descent. People who are multi-racial may also have ancestors more than one of the European groups, and among more than one African nation as well.\n</p><p>Puerto Rico was ceded by <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> in the aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War">Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War</a> under the terms of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_of_1898" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Paris of 1898">Treaty of Paris of 1898</a> and became a territory of the United States. In 1899, the United States conducted its first <a href="/wiki/Census" title="Census">census</a> of Puerto Rico finding that the population of Arecibo was 36,910.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Government">Government</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arecibo,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Government"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Mayoralty_in_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Mayoralty in Puerto Rico">Mayoralty in Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<p>All municipalities in Puerto Rico are administered by a <a href="/wiki/Mayor" title="Mayor">mayor</a>, elected every four years. The current mayor of Arecibo is <a href="/w/index.php?title=Carlos_(Tito)_Ram%C3%ADrez_Irizarri&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Carlos (Tito) Ram\xc3\xadrez Irizarri (page does not exist)">Carlos (Tito) Ram\xc3\xadrez Irizarri</a>, of the <a href="/wiki/Popular_Democratic_Party_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Popular Democratic Party (Puerto Rico)">Popular Democratic Party</a> (PPD). He was elected at the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_general_election,_2020" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rican general election, 2020">2020 general elections</a>.\n</p><p>The city belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Senatorial_district_III" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rico Senatorial district III">Puerto Rico Senatorial district III</a>, which is represented by two Senators. In <a href="/wiki/2012_Puerto_Rican_general_election" title="2012 Puerto Rican general election">2012</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_P%C3%A9rez_Rosa" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 P\xc3\xa9rez Rosa">Jos\xc3\xa9 P\xc3\xa9rez Rosa</a> (<a href="/wiki/New_Progressive_Party_(Puerto_Rico)" title="New Progressive Party (Puerto Rico)">PNP</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Angel_Mart%C3%ADnez_Santiago" class="mw-redirect" title="Angel Mart\xc3\xadnez Santiago">Angel Mart\xc3\xadnez</a> (<a href="/wiki/New_Progressive_Party_(Puerto_Rico)" title="New Progressive Party (Puerto Rico)">PNP</a>) were elected as District Senators,<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and they were re-elected in <a href="/wiki/2016_Puerto_Rican_general_election" title="2016 Puerto Rican general election">2016</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/2020_Puerto_Rican_general_election" title="2020 Puerto Rican general election">2020</a> <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Rosa_V%C3%A9lez" title="Elizabeth Rosa V\xc3\xa9lez">Elizabeth Rosa V\xc3\xa9lez</a> (<a href="/wiki/Popular_Democratic_Party_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Popular Democratic Party (Puerto Rico)">PPD</a>) and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rub%C3%A9n_Soto_Rivera&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Rub\xc3\xa9n Soto Rivera (page does not exist)">Rub\xc3\xa9n Soto Rivera</a> (<a href="/wiki/Popular_Democratic_Party_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Popular Democratic Party (Puerto Rico)">PPD</a>) were elected as District Senators and are the current Senators of this Senatorial district.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Symbols">Symbols</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arecibo,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Symbols"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">municipio</i></span> has an official flag and coat of arms.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The flag and coat of arms were adopted in 1968 with Resolution 12 passed by the government of Arecibo.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Flag">Flag</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arecibo,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Flag"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The flag of <a href="/wiki/Arecibo" class="mw-redirect" title="Arecibo">Arecibo</a> derives its composition and colors from the coat of arms of the city. It is divided vertically in two equal parts. The left side is blue having a belt that stands for "Captain Correa", a local military hero from Spanish times. The right side is made up of blue and yellow diamonds alternating in a checkerboard pattern referring to the coat of arms of Felipe de Beaumont y Navarra, governor of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> (1614\xe2\x80\x931620) and founder of the city. The crown represents The Cacique (chieftain) Arasibo (Fransico Jamaica Arasibo). The turtles represent the ancientness of the city (the third city of Puerto Rico) also because of the indigenous people of the region and that the hunting of turtles was a source of wealth. The towers were a form to describe the population of a settlement. Three towers represent a municipality, four towers represent a village, and five towers represent a city.<sup id="cite_ref-PR_Ency_Founding_Symbols_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PR_Ency_Founding_Symbols-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Coat_of_arms">Coat of arms</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arecibo,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Coat of arms"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The shield is divided by diagonal lines in golden and blue rhombuses with a blue stripe in the superior part, in which resides an opened five-point crown and which is adorned with drawings characterizing the art of the Ta\xc3\xadnos. The people of Arecibo also honored Captain <a href="/wiki/Antonio_de_los_Reyes_Correa" title="Antonio de los Reyes Correa">Antonio de los Reyes Correa</a> by including a gold colored belt in their coat of arms with the words "Muy Leal", which means "Very Faithful", in representation of Correa.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This combination of symbols represents the Indian <a href="/wiki/Cacique" title="Cacique">Cacique</a> (Chieftain) from whom the population\'s name derives, the governor that erected the town and the hero Captain Correa who defended the town from a British invasion.<sup id="cite_ref-PR_Ency_Founding_Symbols_7-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PR_Ency_Founding_Symbols-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Nicknames">Nicknames</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arecibo,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Nicknames"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Arecibo is known as <i>"La Villa del Capit\xc3\xa1n Correa"</i> (Captain Correa\'s Villa) after the Puerto Rican hero <a href="/wiki/Captain_(land)" class="mw-redirect" title="Captain (land)">Captain</a> <a href="/wiki/Antonio_de_los_Reyes_Correa" title="Antonio de los Reyes Correa">Antonio de los Reyes Correa</a> of the Spanish Army, who drove off a <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">British</a> Navy invasion by ambushing forces led by rear-admiral <a href="/wiki/William_Whetstone" title="William Whetstone">William Whetstone</a>. Arecibo is also known as <i>"El Diamante Del Norte"</i> (The Diamond of the North).\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Transportation">Transportation</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arecibo,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Transportation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Puente_Victor_Rojas,_Arecibo,_Puerto_Rico_-_panoramio.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Puente_Victor_Rojas%2C_Arecibo%2C_Puerto_Rico_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-Puente_Victor_Rojas%2C_Arecibo%2C_Puerto_Rico_-_panoramio.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Puente_Victor_Rojas%2C_Arecibo%2C_Puerto_Rico_-_panoramio.jpg/330px-Puente_Victor_Rojas%2C_Arecibo%2C_Puerto_Rico_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Puente_Victor_Rojas%2C_Arecibo%2C_Puerto_Rico_-_panoramio.jpg/440px-Puente_Victor_Rojas%2C_Arecibo%2C_Puerto_Rico_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a><figcaption>Victor Rojas Bridge, had collapsed in 1998 with the forces from Hurricane Georges</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Arecibo has a small noncommercial airport, named <a href="/wiki/Antonio_(Nery)_Juarbe_Pol_Airport" title="Antonio (Nery) Juarbe Pol Airport">Antonio (Nery) Juarbe Pol Airport</a>, which currently has no <a href="/wiki/Airlines" class="mw-redirect" title="Airlines">commercial airline</a> flights.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/PR-22" class="mw-redirect" title="PR-22">PR-22</a> (unsigned Interstate PR-2) passes through the city, but bypasses downtown. Downtown can be accessed via <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_2" title="Puerto Rico Highway 2">PR-2</a>, <a href="/wiki/PR-10" class="mw-redirect" title="PR-10">PR-10</a> and <a href="/wiki/PR-129" class="mw-redirect" title="PR-129">PR-129</a>.\n</p><p>There are 51 bridges in Arecibo.<sup id="cite_ref-bridge_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bridge-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Puente Victor Rojas</i></span> collapsed during <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Georges" title="Hurricane Georges">Hurricane Georges</a> in 1998 but was rebuilt.<sup id="cite_ref-Flood_of_1998_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flood_of_1998-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Despite it being an important bridge leading into the urban downtown center of Arecibo, it was closed again in early 2017 due to damage caused by the sea and reopened in 2021 after repairs.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Education">Education</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arecibo,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Education"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:High_school_in_Arecibo,_Puerto_Rico_(1920)_-_photograph_-_page_147.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/High_school_in_Arecibo%2C_Puerto_Rico_%281920%29_-_photograph_-_page_147.jpg/220px-High_school_in_Arecibo%2C_Puerto_Rico_%281920%29_-_photograph_-_page_147.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/High_school_in_Arecibo%2C_Puerto_Rico_%281920%29_-_photograph_-_page_147.jpg/330px-High_school_in_Arecibo%2C_Puerto_Rico_%281920%29_-_photograph_-_page_147.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/High_school_in_Arecibo%2C_Puerto_Rico_%281920%29_-_photograph_-_page_147.jpg/440px-High_school_in_Arecibo%2C_Puerto_Rico_%281920%29_-_photograph_-_page_147.jpg 2x" data-file-width="526" data-file-height="350" /></a><figcaption>A high school in Arecibo, <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">&#8201;1920</span></figcaption></figure>\n<p>The first school in Arecibo was established on October 12, 1805.<sup id="cite_ref-Cr\xc3\xb3nicas_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cr\xc3\xb3nicas-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Today, Arecibo is home to several public and private schools distributed through its barrios. Public education is handled by the State Department of Education. There are also several colleges and universities located in the city including:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Puerto_Rico_at_Arecibo" title="University of Puerto Rico at Arecibo">University of Puerto Rico at Arecibo</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Interamerican_University_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Interamerican University of Puerto Rico">Interamerican University of Puerto Rico</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Pontifical_Catholic_University_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Pontifical Catholic University of Puerto Rico">Pontifical Catholic University of Puerto Rico</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/National_University_College" title="National University College">National University College</a></li></ul>\n<p>It also has several other technical institutions like ICPR Junior College.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Notable_people">Notable people</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a
